على الأخوات والخالات لأنها من الأمهات ولهذا تحرز من ميراثهن السدس ولأنها أوفر شفقة للأولاد، وأما قوله عليه الصلاة والسلام في حديث أبي داود إنما الخالة أم (۱) فيحتمل كونه في ثبوت الحضانة أو غيره إلا أن السياق أفاد إرادة الأول فيبقى أعم من كونه في ثبوت أصل الحضانة أو كونها أحق بالولد من كل من سواها، ولا دلالة على الثاني والأول متيقن فيثبت فلا يفيد الحكم بكونها أحق من أحد بخصوصه أصلا. ممن له حق في الحضانة فيبقى المعنى الذي عيناه بلا معارض من أن الجدة أم ؛ كذا في فتح القدير وفي القنية : صغيرة عند جدة تخون حقها فلعمها أن يأخذها منها إذا ظهرت خيانتها .
قوله : (ثم الأخت لأب وأم ثم لأم ثم لأب) يعني فهن أولى من العمات والخالات لأنهن بنات الأبوين ولهذا قدمن في الميراث. وتقدم الأخت الشقيقة لأنها أشفق ثم يليها الأخت من الأم لأن الحق لهن من قبل الأم، وأما الأخت لأب فذكر المصنف أنها مقدمة على الخالة اعتباراً لقرب القرابة وتقديم المدلي بالأم على المدلي بالأب عند اتحاد مرتبتهما قرباً وهذه رواية كتاب النكاح وفي رواية كتاب الطلاق الخالة أولى لأنها تدلي بالأم وتلك بالأب. ولم يذكر المصنف أولاد الأخوات لأن فيهم تفصيلاً فأولاد الأخوات لأب وأم أو لأم أحق من الخالات والعمات باتفاق الروايات وأما أولاد الأخوات لأب ففي أحد الروايتين أحق من الخالات اعتباراً بالأصل والصحيح أن الخالات أولى من أولاد الأخوات لأب، والأخت لأم أولى من ولد الأخت لأب وأم وبنات الأخت أولى من بنات الأخ لأن الأخت لها حق في الحضانة دون الأخ فكان المدلي لها أولى، وإذا اجتمع من له حق الحضانة في درجة فأورعهم أولى ثم أكبرهم قوله : (ثم) الخالات كذلك أي فهن أولى من العمات ترجيحاً لقرابة الأم وينزلن كما نزلت الأخوات، فترجح الخالات لأب وأم ثم لأم ثم لأب وهو المراد بقوله كذلك». والخالة هي أخت أم الصغير لا مطلق الخالة لأن خالة الأم مؤخرة عن عمة الصغير وكذلك خالة الأب كما سنبينه. وأفاد كلامه أن الخالة أولى من بنت الأخ لأنها تدلي بالأم وتلك بالأخ قوله : (ثم العمات كذلك) أي تقدم العمة لأب وأم ثم لأم ثم لأب، ولم يذكر المصنف بعد العمات أحداً من النساء، والمذكور في غاية البيان وفتح القدير وغيرهما أن بعد العمات خالة الأم لأب وأم ثم لأم ثم لأب ثم بعدهن خالة الأب لأب وأم ثم لأم ثم لأب زيادة .
قوله : (كما سيأتي أي في الباب الآتي في شرح قول المصنف وهي أحق بعدها ما لم تطلب حقها ثم تعود بالفرقة ثم العصبات بترتيبهم والأم والجدة أحق بالغلام حتى يستغني ثم بعدهن عمات الأمهات والآباء على هذا التفصيل الترتيب. ولم يذكر المصنف أيضاً بنات الأخ وفي التبيين أن بنات الأخ أولى من العمات. ولم يذكر أيضاً أولاد الخالة والعمة في الحضانة لأنه لا حق لبنات العمة والخالة في الحضانة لأنهن غير محرم، وكذلك بنات الأعمام والأخوال بالأولى؛ كذا في كثير من الكتب. وفي غاية البيان والعمة أحق من ولد الخالة . وهو تسامح لأنه لا حق لولد الخالة أصلاً كما نقلناه
Regarding sisters and maternal aunts: because they are from the mothers, and for this reason they inherit one-sixth, and because they have more affection for the children. As for his statement (peace be upon him) in the hadith of Abu Dawud, 'The maternal aunt is a mother,' it is possible that it refers to establishing custody or something else, but the context indicates the first meaning, so it remains general whether it is about establishing the right of custody or that she is more entitled to the child than everyone else. There is no indication of the second, and the first is certain, so it does not benefit the ruling that she is more entitled than any specific person. Those who have a right to custody remain as we determined without opposition: the grandmother is a mother. This is in Fath al-Qadir and in al-Qunyah: a young girl with a grandmother who betrays her trust, her paternal uncle may take her from her if her treachery appears. 
His statement: 'Then the full sister, then the uterine sister, then the consanguine sister' means they are preferred over paternal aunts and maternal aunts because they are daughters of the parents, and for this reason they are given precedence in inheritance. The full sister is given precedence because she is more affectionate, then the uterine sister because her right is from the mother. As for the consanguine sister, the author mentions that she is given precedence over the maternal aunt due to closeness of kinship and giving precedence to the one who connects through the mother over the one who connects through the father when their degrees are equal in closeness. This is the narration in Kitab al-Nikah, while in the narration of Kitab al-Talaq the maternal aunt is given precedence because she connects through the mother while the consanguine sister connects through the father. The author did not mention the daughters of sisters because there is a detail: the daughters of a full or uterine sister are more entitled than maternal and paternal aunts by agreement of all narrations. As for daughters of a consanguine sister, in one of the two narrations they are more entitled than maternal aunts due to considering the original, but the correct view is that maternal aunts are more entitled than daughters of a consanguine sister. A uterine sister is more entitled than the daughter of a full or uterine sister's daughter. Daughters of a sister are more entitled than daughters of a brother because the sister has a right to custody while the brother does not, so the one who connects through her is more entitled. When those who have a right to custody meet at the same degree, the most pious among them is given precedence, then the eldest. 
His statement: 'Then the maternal aunts likewise' means they are more entitled than paternal aunts, giving preference to the mother's side, and they are ranked as the sisters were ranked, so maternal aunts from both parents are given precedence, then from the mother only, then from the father only. That is what is meant by 'likewise.' The maternal aunt is the sister of the young child's mother, not an absolute maternal aunt, because the maternal aunt of the mother is postponed behind the paternal aunt of the child, and likewise the maternal aunt of the father, as we will explain. His statement implies that the maternal aunt is more entitled than the daughter of a brother because she connects through the mother while the other connects through the brother. 
His statement: 'Then the paternal aunts likewise' means a paternal aunt from both parents is given precedence, then from the mother, then from the father. The author did not mention any woman after the paternal aunts. In Ghayat al-Bayan, Fath al-Qadir, and others, it is mentioned that after the paternal aunts comes the maternal aunt of the mother (from both parents, then mother, then father), then after them the maternal aunt of the father (from both parents, then mother, then father) as an addition. 
His statement: 'As will come in the next chapter explaining the author's statement: She is more entitled after that as long as she does not seek...' [text continues]
Source pages p. 284

Commentary
This passage from Al-Bahr al-Raiq Sharh Kanz al-Daqaiq elaborates on the hierarchy of female relatives entitled to custody (hadanah) of a child after dissolution of marriage. The commentary begins by addressing a hadith about the maternal aunt (khala) being like a mother, and clarifies that the hadith establishes her basic right to custody but does not automatically make her more entitled than every other female relative. The author then explains the order as given in the matn: grandmothers are first (with the maternal grandmother preferred over the paternal), then sisters in order: full sister, uterine sister, then consanguine sister. The commentary notes a difference between two narrations: in one the consanguine sister is ahead of the maternal aunt, in another the maternal aunt is ahead. The discussion extends to daughters of sisters, aunts, etc., with the general principle that those connecting through the mother are preferred over those through the father. The text also mentions that the author omitted certain relatives like daughters of brothers because they are not mahram and thus have no right. Finally, the passage notes that if multiple eligible custodians are at the same level, the most pious and then the eldest is chosen.

Key Terms
حضانة (hadanah): The right and duty of a woman to care for and raise the child after separation of parents.
خالة (khālah): Maternal aunt (sister of the child's mother).
عمة (ʿammah): Paternal aunt (sister of the child's father).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi hierarchy in this lesson, who is given precedence between a full sister and a uterine sister?
A) The full sister is given precedence because she is more affectionate.
B) The uterine sister is given precedence because she connects through the mother.
C) They are equal and the choice is left to the judge.
D) The consanguine sister is given precedence over both.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi hierarchy of female custodians prioritizes maternal relatives, with grandmothers first, then sisters, then maternal aunts, then paternal aunts, and certain intra-madhhab disputes exist.

Loss of Female Custody by Marriage to a Non-Mahram
Explains loss and return of custody with proof and ikhtilaf.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling that a female custodian loses hadanah upon marrying a non-mahram, identify the hadith proof, and apply the conditions for loss and return of custody.

Core Idea
A mother's marriage to a non-mahram terminates her custody; only a final divorce restores it.

The right of custody (hadanah) is granted to the mother as long as it serves the child's welfare. However, if she marries a man who is a stranger (non-mahram) to the child, her right is lost due to the potential harm from a stepfather. This lesson examines the textual proof from the hadith, the rationale of harm, and the nuanced rules regarding when custody returns.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is the mother (or female custodian) marrying a man who is not a mahram to the child. The ruling: her right to custody is lost immediately upon the marriage contract.
2
Locate the primary dalil
The hadith: 'أنت أحق به ما لم تتزوجي' (You are more entitled to him as long as you do not marry). This is the core textual evidence.
3
Analyze the wajh al-dalalah
The phrase 'ما لم تتزوجي' (as long as you do not marry) explicitly makes the right conditional on not marrying. Marriage is the terminating event.
4
Note the ikhtilaf on qiyas
The author extends the ruling by qiyas to a custodian residing with a stranger without marriage, based on the common illa of harm. Al-Ramli objects, arguing the hadith specifies marriage and the harm described is unique to a stepfather.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Practical consequence: If a maternal aunt (non-married) lives with a stranger to the child, does she lose custody? Author says yes; al-Ramli says no. The mufta bihi follows the literal hadith.

Source Text

Source pages p. 285

Commentary
This passage deals with the loss of custody (hadanah) when a female custodian (e.g., mother) marries a man who is not a mahram to the child. The ruling is based on a hadith: 'You are more entitled to him as long as you do not marry.' The harm to the child is the reason: a stepfather who is a stranger will treat the child poorly. The commentary clarifies that custody is lost either by actually marrying a non-mahram or by residing in a house where the child is harmed, as in the example of the grandmother residing in her daughter's new husband's house. There is a difference of opinion regarding whether a custodian who is not married but resides with a stranger also loses custody; the author leans towards yes by analogy. The passage also discusses that the husband must be a non-mahram relative; if he is a mahram (like grandfather), the right is not lost. The return of custody occurs only after a final (bain) divorce, not during a revocable divorce until the iddah ends. Finally, there is a note from al-Ramli that 'non-mahram' refers to lineage only, not rada' (foster relationships), and that marriage includes both consummated and unconsummated contracts.

Key Terms
غير محرم (ghayr mahram): A person who is not a mahram (unmarriageable kin) to the child, i.e., a stranger or someone not within the prohibited degrees of marriage.
بائن (bāʾin): Irrevocable divorce that ends the marriage immediately; after such divorce, the husband cannot take back the wife without a new marriage contract.
رجعي (rajʿī): Revocable divorce where the husband can take back the wife during the waiting period without a new marriage.

Key Terms from Source Passage

D) Only if the ex-husband consents.

Key Takeaway
A mother's marriage to a non-mahram ends her custody; only a bain divorce restores it; residence without marriage is disputed.

Mother's Custody Right Lost by Marriage to Non-Mahram
Expansion probe: mother's custody right falls upon marriage to a non-mahram.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the condition under which a mother loses her right to custody, identify the proof (dalil) from the hadith, and explain why marriage to a non-mahram causes the drop.

Core Idea
A mother's right to custody falls when she marries a non-mahram to the child, as established by the hadith and the principle of preventing harm.

This lesson examines the critical ruling that a mother's custody right is lost when she marries a man who is not a mahram to the child. The passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq expands on the matn from Kanz al-Daqa'iq, providing both the textual proof from the hadith and the rational basis (illa) that a non-mahram stepfather will cause harm. We will unpack the conditions, the exceptions, and the cross-madhhab dimension.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Act and Ruling
The act in question is the mother's right to custody (hadana). The ruling is that this right falls (sakat) when she marries a non-mahram to the child. The hukm level is that custody becomes invalid, i.e., she no longer has the right.
The ruling is conditional: only marriage to a non-mahram triggers the loss, not any marriage.
2
Locate the Dalil
The primary proof is the hadith: 'You are more entitled to him as long as you do not marry' (أنت أحق به ما لم تتزوجي). This is a sunnah ahad (zanni al-thubut) but its meaning is clear (qati al-dalala): it explicitly conditions the mother's right on not marrying.
The second proof is rational (ma'qul): a non-mahram stepfather will harm the child by giving little and looking with hatred.
3
Analyze the Conditions and Exceptions
The condition is that the new husband is not a mahram to the child. If he is a mahram (e.g., grandfather, paternal uncle), the right does not fall because no harm exists. The passage also discusses that merely living with a stranger (without marriage) may also cause loss, though the author hesitates.
The key distinction is mahram to the child, not to the mother.
4
Examine the Practical Extensions
The passage extends the ruling to other female custodians like the maternal aunt, and discusses the rent for the child's dwelling, where there are differing views. Also, if the mother denies marriage, her statement is accepted with an oath.
The extensions show how the ruling applies in various scenarios, indicating the richness of fiqh.
5
Compare with Other Schools
The Hanafi position is that the mother's right falls automatically upon marriage to a non-mahram. The Shafi'i school holds that the mother does not lose custody by marriage alone; only if the new husband is harmful. This is a legitimate ikhtilaf rooted in different usul evaluations.
Understanding this difference highlights the importance of the illa (harm) in Hanafi reasoning.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

Source pages p. 285

Commentary
This passage is an expansion probe on the matn statement 'Whoever marries a non-mahram, her right falls' from Kanz al-Daqa'iq. The commentator begins by giving an overview of the entire chapter on custody, listing the order of entitlement: the mother's right, then its return after separation, then the agnates in order, with specific mention of the mother and grandmother having rights over a boy until he becomes independent. He then notes omissions from the matn regarding female relatives, such as daughters of brother being more entitled than paternal aunts, and that children of maternal or paternal aunts have no right at all because they are not mahrams. The core of the lesson is the ruling that a mother's right to custody is lost when she marries a man who is not a mahram to the child. The proof is the hadith 'You are more entitled to him as long as you do not marry' and the rational basis (illa) that a non-mahram stepfather will harm the child by giving little and looking with hatred. The commentator elaborates that custody falls either by marriage to a non-mahram or by the mother living with someone who hates the child. He then discusses a point of hesitation: whether a maternal aunt living with a stranger without being married loses her custody by analogy to a grandmother living with her married daughter. He prefers the first view (that it does fall) because the child is harmed by living in a stranger's house. There is also a discussion about the rent for the child's dwelling, with differing views. The passage emphasizes that if the husband is a mahram (e.g., grandfather, paternal uncle), the mother's right does not fall because there is no harm. It also covers the case where the mother denies marriage, ruling that her statement is accepted with an oath.

Key Terms
حضانة (ḥaḍānah): The right to physically care for and raise a child, including daily needs and supervision.
محرم (maḥram): A person with whom marriage is permanently forbidden due to blood relationship (e.g., father, brother, uncle) or certain other relationships (e.g., fosterage).
نزر (nazr): A small, insignificant amount.
شزر (shazr): A look of hatred or anger.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) If she marries any man, even a mahram to the child.
B) If she marries a man who is a non-mahram to the child.
C) Only if she marries a man who is a mahram to herself.
D) Only if she moves into a house with a stranger.

Key Takeaway
A mother's right to custody falls when she marries a non-mahram to the child, based on the hadith and the principle of preventing harm, and this is the mufta bihi position in the Hanafi school.

Talaq — Divorce

Return of Custody Upon Bain Divorce
Commentary on matn: custody returns upon bain divorce.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on when a mother's custody right returns after marriage to a non-mahram and distinguish between bain and raj'i divorce.

Core Idea
Custody returns immediately upon bain divorce; raj'i divorce requires iddah to expire.

In this lesson, we examine a passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq explaining the matn phrase 'then it returns by separation.' The commentator clarifies that the mother's custody right, which fell due to marriage to a non-mahram, is restored when the marriage ends, but only if the divorce is bain (irrevocable). We will unpack the distinction, the analogy with the nashiz wife, and the conditions regarding mahram relationships and consummation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core ruling
Determine the general rule: custody returns when the impediment (marriage to a non-mahram) is removed by separation. The separation must be a definitive end to the marriage.
The passage specifies bain divorce, not raj'i.
2
Distinguish bain from raj'i
Bain divorce severs the marriage tie completely, so the impediment is removed immediately. Raj'i divorce does not end the marriage until iddah expires, so custody does not return until then.
The marriage tie (zawjiyyah) remains during iddah in raj'i divorce.
3
Understand the impediment removal metaphor
The custody right was not abolished but merely obstructed, like the nashiz wife loses maintenance while disobedient but regains it when she returns home.
The falling of the right is due to a temporary impediment, not a permanent loss.
4
Analyze the mahram condition
The mother's marriage to a non-mahram (including foster mahram) causes the right to fall. It does not matter if consummation occurred or not; the contract alone suffices.
Blood mahram marriages do not cause the right to fall because the mother remains a mahram to the child.
5
Evaluate the scenario of disputed divorce
If the mother admits to marriage but claims divorce, her word is accepted if she does not specify the husband; if she names him, her claim of divorce is not accepted.
This relates to legal presumption and burden of proof.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (ثم تعود بالفرقة) أي تعود الحضانة لزوال المانع فقولهم سقط حقها» معناه منع مانع منه لأنه من باب زوال المانع لا من عود الساقط كالناشزة لا نفقة لها ثم تعود بالعود إلى منزل الزوج. وأراد بالفرقة الطلاق البائن، وأما الطلاق الرجعي فإنه لا يعود حقها به حتى تنقضي عدتها لقيام الزوجية. وفي الظهيرية كما : قول المصنف : (ومن نكحت غير محرمة سقط حقها قال الرملي : يعني محرمة النسبي لا الرضاعي فإنه كالأجنبي في سقوط حضانتها به فكان ينبغي أن يقول غير محرمة الرحم تأمل قوله : كالأم إذا تزوجت بأجنبي عنه قال الرملي : سواء دخل بها أو لم يدخل لأن التزوج اسم للعقد ولا يتوقف السقوط على الدخول قوله : (والذي يظهر الأول الخ ) قال الرملي : بل الذي يظهر الثاني لقولهم يطعمه نزراً وينظر إليه شزراً وهذا مفقود في الأجنبي عن الحاضنة، والحديث قد غياه بغاية وهي التزوج فيستمر الحق إلى وجوده ولم يوجد تأمل. ثم رأيت صاحب النهر قال بعد نقله لما . وغيرها : لو أقرت بالتزوج وادعت أنه طلقها وعاد حقها فيها فإن أبهمت الزوج كان القول قولها، وإن عينت لا يقبل قولها في دعوى الطلاق. من محارمه من النساء
His saying: (Then it returns by separation) i.e., custody returns due to the removal of the impediment. So their saying 'her right fell' means an impediment prevented it, because it is a case of removal of impediment, not return of a fallen right, like the nashiz (disobedient wife) has no maintenance, then it returns by returning to the husband's home. And he intended by separation the bain (irrevocable) divorce. As for raj'i (revocable) divorce, her right does not return by it until her iddah expires due to the existence of the marriage tie. And in al-Zahiriyyah: the author's saying (And whoever marries a non-mahram, her right falls.) al-Ramli said: meaning a blood mahram, not a foster mahram, for the latter is like a stranger in that her custody falls thereby, so it would have been better for him to say 'non-mahram of the womb'. He said: 'like the mother when she marries a stranger to him' - al-Ramli said: whether he consummated the marriage or not, because marriage is the name of the contract, and the falling does not depend on consummation. His saying: (And what appears is the first etc.) al-Ramli said: rather what appears is the second, because of their saying 'he feeds him little and looks at him with hatred' and this is lacking in the stranger to the custodian, and the hadith has limited it to a limit which is marriage, so the right continues until it occurs, and it did not occur. Then I saw the author of al-Nahr said after quoting what... And other than that: If she admits to marriage and claims that he divorced her and her right returned, then if she ambiguates the husband, her statement is accepted, and if she specifies, her statement regarding the claim of divorce is not accepted. From his female mahrams.
Source pages p. 285

Commentary
This passage is an expansion probe on the matn phrase 'then it returns by separation.' The commentator explains that the mother's custody right, which had fallen due to marriage to a non-mahram, returns when the marriage ends. This is not a return of a fallen right but rather the removal of the impediment, akin to a nashiz wife regaining maintenance. Separation here means bain (irrevocable) divorce; a raj'i divorce does not restore the right until the iddah expires because the marriage tie still exists. The passage then includes quotes from al-Ramli discussing the classification of mahram (blood vs. foster) and the condition of consummation. It also addresses a scenario where the mother admits to marriage but claims divorce: if she does not specify the husband, her claim is accepted; if she names him, her claim of divorce is not accepted. The passage ends with a brief note on male mahrams.

Key Terms
فرقة (furqah): Separation by divorce, specifically bain (irrevocable) divorce in this context.
بائن (bā'in): An irrevocable divorce that ends the marriage immediately, after which the husband cannot take the wife back without a new marriage.
ناشزة (nāshizah): A wife who is disobedient and leaves the marital home without valid reason, losing her right to maintenance.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In which type of divorce does the mother's custody right immediately return?
A) Raj'i divorce
B) Bain divorce
C) Both types
D) Neither type

Key Takeaway
Custody returns upon bain divorce because the impediment (marriage to non-mahram) is removed; raj'i divorce only restores it after iddah.

Custody Order Among Agnates and Conditions for Female Custodians
Commentary on agnate custody order and conditions for female custodians

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the order of agnate male custodians for a child in Hanafi law and identify the conditions under which a non-mahram agnate may be given custody of a girl.

Core Idea
For boy custody, agnate order applies; for girls, non-mahram agnates are excluded unless no fitna risk.

This passage from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq expands on the matn ruling that after female relatives, custody goes to the agnates in order of closeness. However, the rule is not absolute for girls: the risk of fitna (temptation) restricts giving a girl to a non-mahram male. The commentator also discusses an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf regarding whether a maternal uncle (mahram) should be preferred over a cousin (agnate) for custody of a girl.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Ruling: Order of Agnates for Custody
Recognize that the passage states the order of male agnates: father, grandfather, full brother, consanguine brother, their sons, then paternal uncles and their sons. This order applies when the child has no female custodian.
The order is based on closeness by agnation (ta'sib).
2
Distinguish Between Boy and Girl Custody
Note that for a boy, any male agnate can take custody, even if not mahram, because there is no fear of fitna. For a girl, non-mahram agnates (like cousins) are generally excluded.
Fitna is the key factor for girls.
3
Identify Exceptions to the Exclusion of Non-Mahram Agnates for Girls
The commentator qualifies the general rule: if the girl is very young (e.g., one year old) and not yet desirable, or if the agnate is trustworthy (mamun), then custody may be given. The judge has discretion to appoint the cousin if suitable, otherwise a trustworthy woman.
This shows the ruling is not rigid; it depends on circumstances.
4
Analyze the Intra-Hanafi Dispute: Cousin vs Maternal Uncle
Imam Muhammad holds that if a girl has both a cousin and a maternal uncle (both trustworthy), the maternal uncle is preferred because he is a mahram. Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf prioritize the cousin as an agnate. The commentator leans towards Muhammad's view as a new fatwa.
This ikhtilaf shows the tension between agnation and mahramiyya.
5
Apply the Condition of Adulthood for Custodians
The passage confirms that custody is a type of guardianship (wilayah), so the custodian must be an adult. A minor cannot be a custodian.
This is a general condition for any custodian.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (ثم العصبات بترتيبهم يعني إن لم يكن للصغير أحد واختصم فيه الرجال فأولاهم به أقربهم تعصيباً لأن الولاية للأقرب فيقدم الأب ثم الجد أب الأب وإن علا ثم الأخ الشقيق ثم الأخ لأب ثم ابن الأخ الشقيق ثم ابن الأخ لأب، وكذا كل من سفل من أولادهم ثم العم شقيق الأب ثم لأب وأما أولاد الأعمام فإنه يدفع إليهم الغلام فيبدأ بابن العم لأب وأم ثم ابن العم لأب، ولا تدفع إليهم الصغيرة لأنهم غير محارم، وكذا لا تدفع إلى الأم التي ليست بمأمونة وللعصبة الفاسق ولا إلى مولى العتاقة تحرزاً عن الفتنة. وبهذا علم أن إطلاق المصنف في محل التقييد لكن ينبغي أن يكون محل عدم الدفع إلى ابن العم ما إذا كانت الصغيرة تشتهي وهو غير مأمون أما إذا كانت لا تشتهي كبنت سنة مثلاً فلا منع لأنه لا فتنة، وكذا إذا كانت تشتهي وكان مأموناً. قال في غاية البيان معزياً إلى تحفة الفقهاء : وإن لم يكن للجارية من عصباتها غير ابن العم فالاختيار إلى القاضي إن رآه أصلح تضم إليه وإلا توضع على يد أمينة ا هـ . ولم يذكر المصنف الدفع إلى ذوي الأرحام : البحر أقول : الظاهر عدم سقوطها للفرق البين بين زوج الأم والأجنبي ا هـ. قوله : (يعني إن لم يكن للصغير أحد الخ) قال الرملي أو كان له أحد من محارمه من النساء إلا أنه ساقط الحضانة فإنه كالمعدوم قوله : (فإنه يدفع إليهم الغلام لأن عدم المحرمية مع اتحاد الجنس لا يخاف منه الفتنة، ومقتضى هذا أن تدفع الأنثى إلى بنت العم للعلة المذكورة لكنه خلاف إطلاقه السابق في ذوات الأرحام فتأمل. بقي هنا فائدة وهي أنه لو كان للغلام ابنا عم أحدهما زوج أمه وليس له غيرهم فالظاهر أنه لا يسقط حق الأم وإن كان زوجها أجنبياً عن الغلام لأن ابن العم الآخر كذلك قوله : لكن ينبغي أن يكون الخ) قال الرملي هذا البحث مردود لتعليلهم بأن أولاد الأعمام غير محارم للصغير وأنه لا حق لغير المحرم في حضانتها ولعل الوجه فيه أنه لو ثبت له ذلك كانت عنده إلى أن تشتهي فتقع الفتنة فحسم من أصله تأمل هذا ولا شاهد له بما في غاية البيان لأن جواز ضمها لابن العم لا لكونه مستحقاً للحضانة بل لا صلحيته لضمها وإلا لم يكن الاختيار للقاضي، والكلام في استحقاقها لا في جواز الدفع له عند عدم من يستحقها، هذا ويجب أن يقيد كلام التحفة بما إذا لم يكن هناك من ذوي الأرحام بالمعنى المراد من يستحق الحضانة، أما إذا كان كالأخ لأن تدفع إليه لا إلى ابن العم ولو والنظائر ا هـ. قلت : وفي البدائع وقال محمد: إن كان للجارية ابن عم وخال وكلاهما لا بأس به في دينه جعلها القاضي عند الخال لأنه محرم فكان أولى
His saying: (Then the agnates in their order) means if the young child has no one and men contest, then the most entitled is the nearest by agnation, because guardianship belongs to the nearest. So the father is preferred, then the grandfather (father's father) however high, then the full brother, then the consanguine brother, then the son of the full brother, then the son of the consanguine brother, and likewise all descendants, then the full paternal uncle, then the consanguine paternal uncle. As for the sons of paternal uncles, the boy is given to them; they start with the son of the paternal uncle by both parents, then son of the paternal uncle by father only. But the small girl is not given to them because they are not mahram. Likewise, she is not given to a mother who is not trustworthy, nor to a fasiq agnate, nor to the freed slave, to avoid fitna. By this it is known that the author's absolute statement is in need of qualification. But it should be that the case of not giving to the cousin is when the girl is desirable and he is not trustworthy; if she is not desirable like a one-year-old girl, then there is no prohibition because there is no fitna, and likewise if she is desirable and he is trustworthy. It is said in Ghayat al-Bayan quoting Tuhfat al-Fuqaha: If the girl has no agnate besides the cousin, then the choice is for the judge; if he sees him suitable he entrusts her to him, otherwise he places her with a trustworthy woman. The author did not mention giving to the uterine relatives. Al-Bahr says: I say the apparent is that it does not fall due to the clear difference between the stepfather and a stranger. His saying: (means if the young child has no one etc.) al-Ramli said: or he has one of his female mahrams but she has fallen from custody, then she is considered non-existent. His saying: (so the boy is given to them because lack of mahramiyya with same gender does not cause fear of fitna. The implication of this is that the female should be given to the daughter of the paternal uncle for the mentioned reason, but it contradicts his earlier absolute statement about uterine relatives, so reflect. There remains a benefit: if the boy has two cousins, one of whom is the husband of his mother and he has no other, it appears that the mother's right does not fall even if her husband is a stranger to the boy, because the other cousin is also like that. His saying: (but it should be etc.) al-Ramli said: this discussion is rejected because their reasoning is that the sons of paternal uncles are not mahram to the small girl and that there is no right for a non-mahram in her custody. Perhaps the reason is that if he had custody, she would be with him until she becomes desirable and fitna would occur, so it is cut off from the root. Reflect on this, and there is no evidence for it from what is in Ghayat al-Bayan, because permissibility of entrusting her to the cousin is not because he is entitled to custody but because of his suitability; otherwise the judge would not have a choice. The discussion is about entitlement, not permissibility of giving to him when there is no one entitled. This must be qualified by the words of Tuhfa when there is no uterine relative in the intended sense who is entitled to custody. But if there is someone like the maternal uncle, she is given to him, not to the cousin, even if the judge sees him as more suitable, as long as the maternal uncle is not a fasiq, and this is a new fatwa. It is required that the custodian be adult because custody is a type of guardianship, as stated by Ibn Malik in Sharh al-Majma' and others, and a minor is not qualified for guardianship as stated in al-Ashbah wa al-Naza'ir. I say: In al-Bada'i, Muhammad said: If the girl has a cousin and a maternal uncle and both are sound in religion, the judge places her with the maternal uncle because he is a mahram, so he is more entitled.
Source pages p. 286

Commentary
This passage is an expansion probe on the matn 'then the agnates in their order' regarding male relatives' right to custody after the mother and female relatives. The order is: father, grandfather, full brother, consanguine brother, their sons, then paternal uncles and their sons. Boys are given to these agnates even if not mahram, but girls are not given to non-mahram males due to the risk of fitna (temptation). However, the commentator qualifies this: if the girl is very young (e.g., one year old) or if the male is trustworthy, it may be permissible. He cites from Ghayat al-Bayan that if the only agnate is a cousin, the judge decides based on suitability; otherwise, a trustworthy woman is appointed. The passage also discusses the case of a boy having two cousins, one of whom is his mother's new husband; the mother's right does not fall because another cousin exists. There is a debate about whether a female child can be given to a female cousin (bint al-amm); the commentator notes the logical implication but says it contradicts the earlier rule about uterine relatives. Finally, the condition that the custodian must be an adult is affirmed, citing authoritative works. A notable intra-Hanafi difference is mentioned: Muhammad ibn al-Hasan al-Shaybani holds that if the girl has both a cousin and a maternal uncle, the judge should place her with the maternal uncle because he is a mahram.

Key Terms
عصبات (ʿaṣabāt): Male agnate relatives who inherit by virtue of being related through the father's line.
فتنة (fitnah): Temptation or moral corruption that may occur from close contact between non-mahram males and females.
محارم (maḥārim): Plural of mahram: individuals with whom marriage is perpetually forbidden.
ولاية (wilāyah): Guardianship or authority, which requires adulthood and competence. Custody is considered a branch of guardianship.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, when can a girl be given to her cousin (ibn amm) for custody?
A) Always, because he is a close agnate.
B) Only if she is very young and not yet desirable, or if he is trustworthy.
C) Never, because he is not a mahram.
D) Only if there is no other relative.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi custody law, agnates are ordered by closeness, but for girls, non-mahram agnates are excluded unless the girl is very young or the male is trustworthy; the maternal uncle (mahram) is preferred over the cousin.

Order of Male Custodians (Asaba) after Female Relatives
Commentary on the order of male agnates entitled to custody

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi order of male custodians for a child and identify the condition of mahram for a female child.

Core Idea
Male custodians are prioritized by closeness of agnatic relation, but a female child cannot be given to a non-mahram.

This lesson examines the Hanafi ruling on the order of male relatives entitled to custody (hadana) when no female custodian is available. The commentator explains the priority list based on agnatic relationship (ta'sib) and highlights a crucial condition: a young girl must not be placed with a non-mahram male, such as a cousin, to avoid fitna. The lesson also addresses the requirement that the custodian be an adult, as custody is a form of guardianship.

Guided Path
1
Identify the priority order of male custodians
List the male relatives in order: father, grandfather, full brother, half-brother from father, son of full brother, son of half-brother, paternal uncle (full then half), and then their sons (cousins). This order is based on closeness in ta'sib.
The father is always first, followed by ascending male ancestors, then collaterals.
2
Recognize the mahram condition for female children
A young girl is not given to non-mahram males like cousins because of the risk of fitna. However, if she is very young (e.g., one year old) or the male is trustworthy, the restriction may be relaxed at the judge's discretion.
Non-mahram means the male is not permanently prohibited from marrying her.
3
Understand the intra-Hanafi dispute on placement with a cousin
Some later scholars argue a cousin can be custodian if trustworthy, but the relied-upon (mufta bihi) position is that non-mahrams have no right. The judge may place the girl with a cousin only as a suitable arrangement, not due to entitlement.
The dispute is about entitlement vs. suitability.
4
Apply the condition of majority in the custodian
The custodian must be an adult (baligh) because custody is a type of guardianship (wilaya), and a minor cannot exercise guardianship.
This condition is explicitly stated in al-Ashbah wa al-Naza'ir.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

ابن الأخ لأب، وكذا كل من سفل من أولادهم ثم العم شقيق الأب ثم لأب وأما أولاد الأعمام فإنه يدفع إليهم الغلام فيبدأ بابن العم لأب وأم ثم ابن العم لأب، ولا تدفع إليهم الصغيرة لأنهم غير محارم، وكذا لا تدفع إلى الأم التي ليست بمأمونة وللعصبة الفاسق ولا إلى مولى العتاقة تحرزاً عن الفتنة. وبهذا علم أن إطلاق المصنف في محل التقييد لكن ينبغي أن يكون محل عدم الدفع إلى ابن العم ما إذا كانت الصغيرة تشتهي وهو غير القاضي إن رآه أصلح تضم إليه وإلا توضع على يد أمينة ا هـ . ولم يذكر المصنف الدفع إلى ذوي الأرحام : البحر أقول : الظاهر عدم سقوطها للفرق البين بين زوج الأم والأجنبي ا هـ. قوله : (يعني إن لم يكن للصغير أحد الخ) قال الرملي أو كان له أحد من محارمه من النساء إلا أنه ساقط الحضانة فإنه كالمعدوم قوله : (فإنه يدفع إليهم الغلام لأن عدم المحرمية مع اتحاد الجنس لا يخاف منه الفتنة، ومقتضى هذا أن تدفع الأنثى إلى بنت العم للعلة المذكورة لكنه خلاف إطلاقه السابق في ذوات الأرحام فتأمل. بقي هنا فائدة وهي أنه لو كان للغلام ابنا عم أحدهما زوج أمه وليس له غيرهم فالظاهر أنه لا يسقط حق الأم وإن كان زوجها أجنبياً عن الغلام لأن ابن العم الآخر كذلك قوله : لكن ينبغي أن يكون الخ) قال الرملي هذا البحث مردود لتعليلهم بأن أولاد الأعمام غير محارم للصغير وأنه لا حق لغير المحرم في حضانتها ولعل الوجه فيه أنه لو ثبت له ذلك كانت عنده إلى أن تشتهي فتقع الفتنة فحسم من أصله تأمل هذا ولا شاهد له بما في غاية البيان لأن جواز ضمها لابن العم لا لكونه مستحقاً للحضانة بل لا صلحيته لضمها وإلا لم يكن الاختيار للقاضي، والكلام في استحقاقها لا في جواز الدفع له عند عدم من يستحقها، هذا ويجب أن يقيد كلام التحفة بما إذا لم يكن هناك من ذوي الأرحام بالمعنى المراد من يستحق الحضانة، أما إذا كان كالأخ لأن تدفع إليه لا إلى ابن العم ولو والنظائر ا هـ.
His statement: (Then the agnates in their order) meaning if the child has no one [from female relatives] and the men dispute, then the most entitled is the closest in agnatic relationship because guardianship belongs to the nearest. So the father is presented, then the grandfather (father's father) however high, then the full brother, then the half-brother from father, then the son of full brother, then the son of half-brother from father, and likewise everyone descending from them, then the paternal uncle full brother of father, then [paternal uncle] from father. As for the sons of paternal uncles, the boy is given to them, beginning with the cousin from father and mother, then the cousin from father. The young girl is not given to them because they are not mahrams. Likewise, she is not given to the mother who is not trustworthy, nor to a sinful agnate, nor to the freed slave [mawla al-itaqa] to avoid temptation. By this it is known that the author's absolute statement is in a place requiring restriction, but it should be that the place of non-delivery to the cousin is when the young girl is desirous and he is not trustworthy; but if she is not desirous, like a one-year-old girl, then there is no prevention because there is no temptation. Likewise if she is desirous and he is trustworthy. He said in Ghayat al-Bayan, attributing to Tuhfat al-Fuqaha': If the girl has no agnate other than the cousin, then the choice is to the judge: if he sees him as suitable, he places her with him; otherwise, he places her with a trustworthy woman. End quote. And the author did not mention delivery to uterine relatives. Al-Bahr: I say: The apparent is that it does not fall due to the clear difference between the mother's husband and a stranger. End quote. His statement: (meaning if the child has no one etc.) al-Ramli said: Or if he has one of his female mahrams but she has forfeited custody, then she is like non-existent. His statement: (Then he gives the boy to them because with unity of gender, no temptation is feared from non-mahram relationship. The consequence of this is that the female would be given to the daughter of the cousin for the mentioned reason, but that contradicts his previous absolute statement about uterine relatives, so reflect. There remains here a benefit: If the boy has two paternal cousins, one of them is his mother's husband and he has no others, then apparently the mother's right is not dropped even if her husband is a stranger to the boy, because the other cousin is also such. His statement: (But it should be that etc.) al-Ramli said: This research is rejected because of their reasoning that the children of paternal uncles are not mahrams for the girl, and there is no right for a non-mahram in her custody. Perhaps the reason is that if he were granted that, she would be with him until she becomes desirous and temptation occurs, so it is closed from the root. Consider this, and there is no evidence from what is in Ghayat al-Bayan, because the permissibility of placing her with the cousin is not because he is entitled to custody, but because of his suitability for placement; otherwise the judge would have no choice. The discussion is about entitlement, not about permissibility of giving to him when there is no one entitled. This, and it is necessary to restrict the statement of al-Tuhfah to when there is no uterine relative in the intended sense who is entitled to custody. However, if there is one like a brother, then it is given to him, not to the cousin, even if the judge sees the cousin as more suitable, as long as the uterine brother is not sinful, and this is a contemporary fatwa matter. And majority is required in the one who fosters the child because custody is a type of guardianship, as stated by Ibn Malik in Sharh al-Majma' and others, and a minor is not fit for guardianship, as stated in al-Ashbah wa al-Naza'ir. End quote.
Source pages p. 286

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the matn statement 'Then the agnates in their order' from Kanz al-Daqa'iq. The commentator explains the order of male relatives entitled to custody of a child when no female custodian is available or suitable. The order is based on closeness of agnatic relationship (ta'sib). The father is first, then grandfather, then full brother, then half-brother from father, then their sons, then paternal uncles (full then half), then their sons (cousins). A key condition is that a young girl is not given to non-mahram relatives like cousins because of the risk of fitna. However, if the girl is very young (not desirous) or the cousin is trustworthy, the strict rule is relaxed. The text also discusses a scenario where a boy has two cousins, one of whom is his stepfather (his mother's husband). The author concludes that the mother's right is not lost even though her husband is not a mahram to the boy, because the other cousin is also not a mahram. The commentary then addresses a dispute: al-Ramli rejects a previous opinion that a cousin may be entitled to custody of a girl, emphasizing that non-mahrams have no right. He explains that the judge's discretion to place the girl with a cousin is not based on entitlement but on suitability when no entitled custodian exists. The passage concludes by stating that the custodian must be an adult, because custody is a form of guardianship (wilaya), and a minor cannot exercise guardianship. This is a relied-upon ruling (mufta bihi).

Key Terms
عصبة (asaba): Agnatic relatives who inherit by virtue of being male through male line.
محرم (mahram): A person with whom marriage is permanently prohibited due to blood relation, marriage, or suckling.
تعصيب (ta'sib): The principle of agnatic closeness that determines priority among male relatives.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, who is the first male entitled to custody after the female relatives?
A) The grandfather
B) The father
C) The full brother
D) The paternal uncle

Key Takeaway
Male custodians are ordered by agnatic closeness, with the father first, but a female child must not be given to a non-mahram male, and the custodian must be an adult.

Order of Maternal Custody When No Agnate Exists
Explanation of maternal custody order when no agnate exists

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi order of maternal relatives entitled to custody in the absence of agnates and explain the intra-Hanafi dispute regarding male maternal relatives.

Core Idea
Without agnates, the uterine brother is first for custody; maternal relatives follow in an order based on marriage guardianship.

Custody of a young child becomes critical when no agnatic relatives exist. The Hanafi school specifies a clear order of maternal relatives who are entitled—starting with the uterine brother. This passage from Al-Bahr al-Raiq details that order and clarifies the scope of 'dhawu al-arham' in this context. It also notes an important difference of opinion within the school regarding the rights of male maternal relatives.

Guided Path
1
Identify the condition for maternal custody
The text begins 'If the child has no agnate' — this is the prerequisite. Maternal relatives only become entitled in default of any 'asaba (agnatic male relatives).
Agnates include paternal male relatives like father, son, paternal uncle, etc.
2
List the order of maternal relatives
The author gives a sequence: uterine brother, then his son, then maternal uncle (from mother's side), then maternal uncle from both parents, then from father only, then from mother only. Memorize this order as stated.
The uterine brother is a half-brother sharing only the mother.
3
Understand the basis for the order
These maternal relatives have guardianship (wilaya) in marriage according to Abu Hanifa. By analogy (qiyas), they are entitled to custody when no agnate exists.
This analogy links custody to marriage guardianship.
4
Clarify the term 'dhawu al-arham'
The passage explains that here 'dhawu al-arham' includes all non-agnatic relatives, not just those in inheritance law who have no fixed share. For example, the uterine brother is a Quranic share heir but is included in custody.
This broader definition avoids confusion with inheritance terminology.
5
Analyze the intra-Hanafi dispute
Al-Bada'i' states that men from the mother's side have no right to custody. The passage interprets this as applying only when some paternal relative exists. Without any paternal relative, the general order applies.
This nuance affects real cases: if a distant paternal cousin exists, the Bada'i' view might exclude the maternal uncle.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قالوا : إذا لم يكن للصغير عصبة يدفع إلى الأخ لأم ثم إلى ولده ثم إلى العم لأم ثم إلى الخال لأب وأم ثم لأب ثم لأم لأن لهؤلاء ولاية عند أبي حنيفة في النكاح. وبهذا علم أن مرادهم بذوي الأرحام هنا وفي باب ولاية إلا نكاح قرابة ليست بعصبة لا المذكور في الفرائض أنه قريب ليس بذي سهم ولا عصبة لأن بعض أقارب الفروض داخل في ذوي الأرحام هنا كالأخ لأم، وإذا اجتمع مستحقو الحضانة في درجة كالإخوة والأعمام فأصلحهم أولى، فإن تساووا فأورعهم، فإن تساووا فأسنهم. وفي البدائع لا حق للرجال من قبل الأم وهو محمول على ما إذا كان من قبل الأب من هو موجود
They said: If the child has no agnate, he is given to the uterine brother, then to his son, then to the maternal uncle, then to the maternal uncle from father and mother, then from father, then from mother, because these have guardianship in marriage according to Abu Hanifa. By this it is known that their intended meaning of 'uterine relatives' here and in the chapter of guardianship except marriage is relatives who are not agnates, not the one mentioned in inheritance law who is a relative without a fixed share and not an agnate, because some relatives entitled to fixed shares are included among uterine relatives here, like the uterine brother. And when custodians are equal in degree, like brothers and paternal uncles, the most suitable is preferred; if equal, the most pious; if equal, the oldest. And in al-Bada'i', men from the mother's side have no right, and this is interpreted as when there is someone from the father's side present.
Source pages p. 287

Commentary
This passage addresses the situation where a child has no agnatic ('asaba) relatives. In such a case, custody goes to maternal relatives in a specific order: first the uterine brother (half-brother from mother), then his son, then the maternal uncle (mother's brother), then the maternal uncle from both parents (mother's full brother), then from father only (half maternal uncle), then from mother only (maternal half-uncle). This order is based on the principle that these relatives have guardianship (wilaya) in marriage according to Abu Hanifa. The passage clarifies that 'dhawu al-arham' (uterine relatives) here means all non-agnatic blood relatives, which is broader than the inheritance definition. When multiple custodians are at the same level (e.g., several brothers or uncles), the judge chooses the most suitable (aslah), then the most pious (awra'), then the oldest (asann). The commentator notes that according to al-Bada'i', men from the mother's side only have right if no paternal male exists; otherwise, they are excluded. This ruling is from the Hanafi school.

Key Terms
ذوو الأرحام (dhawu al-arham): Uterine relatives; all blood relatives who are not agnates nor Quranic share heirs. In this context, it includes even those with fixed shares (like uterine brother).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
When no agnate exists, who is the first maternal relative entitled to custody according to the passage?
A) The maternal uncle
B) The uterine brother
C) The maternal grandfather
D) The mother's sister

Key Takeaway
In the absence of agnates, custody goes to the uterine brother first, followed by a specific order of maternal relatives, with an intra-Hanafi dispute on male maternal relatives' rights when paternal relatives exist.

Duration of Custody: Mother and Grandmother
Explains duration of mother's custody

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi durations for mother's custody of a boy and a girl, and explain the later fatwa regarding girls.

Core Idea
Custody ends for a boy when independent (7 years); for a girl, the later fatwa shifts her to father at age of desire, not menstruation.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq explains when the mother's (and grandmother's) right to custody (hadanah) ends. For a boy, it is when he becomes independent, estimated at seven years. For a girl, the classical view is until she menstruates, but later Hanafi masters gave fatwa on the view of Imam Muhammad and Abu Yusuf that she should be transferred to the father at the age of sexual desire due to moral corruption. Understanding this nuance is key for applying Hanafi family law today.

Guided Path
1
Identify the general rule for boys
The passage states that the mother/grandmother has custody of a boy until he becomes independent (istighna'), estimated at seven years by al-Khassaf.
The criterion is ability to eat, drink, dress, and clean himself independently.
2
Identify the general rule for girls
The classical rule is custody until the girl menstruates (i.e., reaches puberty).
The reason given is that she needs to learn feminine manners and then needs protection which the father provides.
3
Recognize the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Imam Muhammad and Abu Yusuf opined that the girl should be given to the father when she reaches the age of desire (hadd al-shahwa), earlier than menstruation.
This is due to the need for protection in corrupt times.
4
Determine the mufta bihi position
Later authorities like al-Niqayah and al-Tabyin adopt the view of Muhammad and Abu Yusuf as the operative fatwa.
The reason given is 'corruption of the times' – a socio-legal consideration.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (والأم والجدة أحق بالغلام حتى يستغني وقدر بسبع لأنه إذا استغنى يحتاج إلى تأديب والتخلق بأداب الرجال وأخلاقهم والأب أقدر على التأديب والتعنيف، وما ذكره المصنف من التقدير قول الخصاف اعتباراً بسبع للقالب لأن الظاهر أن الصغير إذا بلغ السبع يهتدي بنفسه إلى الأكل والشرب واللبس والاستنجاء وحده فلا حاجة إلى الحضانة فلا مخالفة بين تقدير الاستغناء بالسن وبين أن على الأشياء الأربعة وحده كما هو المذكور في الأصل، ولم يذكر الاستنجاء في المبسوط وذكره في السير الكبير وزاد في نوادر ابن رشيد ويتوضأ وحده ثم من المشايخ من قال : المراد من الاستنجاء تمام الطهارة بأن يطهر وجهه وحده بلا معين. ومنهم من قال بل من النجاسة وإن لم يقدر على تمام الطهارة وهو المفهوم من ظاهر كلام الخصاف. وفي غاية البيان والتبيين والكافي أن الفتوى على قول الخصاف من التقدير بالسبع لأن الأب مأمور بأن يأمره بالصلاة إذا بلغها وإنما يكون ذلك إذا كان الولد عنده . ولو اختلفا فقال ابن وقالت سبع ابن ست لا يحلف القاضي أحدهما ولكن ينظر إن كان يأكل وحده ويلبس وحده ويستنجي وحده دفع وإلا فلا كذا في الظهيرية. واستغنى بذكر الأكل عن الشرب ولذا ذكر الشرب في الخلاصة وجمع بين الأربعة في التبيين وأما ما في فتح القدير والخلاصة من عدم ذكر الاستنجاء فسهو. وأشار المصنف رحمه الله بذكر الأم والجدة إلى أن غيرهما أولى، فلو قال والحاضنة أحق به حتى يستغني لكان أصرح. · قوله: (وبها حتى تحيض) أي الأم والجدة أحق بالصغيرة حتى تحيض لأن بعد الاستغناء تحتاج إلى معرفة آداب النساء والمرأة على ذلك أقدر، وبعد البلوغ تحتاج إلى التحصين والحفظ والأب فيه أقوى وأهدى وبه علم أنه لو قال حتى تبلغ لكان أولى. وعن محمد أنها تدفع إلى الأب إذا بلغت حد الشهوة لتحقق الحاجة إلى الصيانة قال في النقاية : وهو المعتبر لفساد الزمان . وفي نفقات الخصاف : وعن أبي يوسف مثله. وفي التبيين : وبه يفتى في زماننا. والأخ لأب أحق من الخال لأنه عصبة وأقرب قوله : ( يدفع إلى الأخ لأم الخ) ذكر في الفتاوى الهندية أن أبا الأم أولى من الأخ لأم والخال .
His statement: (And the mother and grandmother have more right to the boy until he becomes independent, and it is estimated at seven years) because when he becomes independent, he needs discipline and to adopt the manners and morals of men, and the father is more capable of discipline and severity. What the author mentioned of estimation is the saying of al-Khassaf, considering seven years as a measurement, because apparently when the child reaches seven, he can guide himself to eating, drinking, dressing, and cleaning himself alone, so there is no need for custody. So there is no contradiction between estimating independence by age and being able to do the four things alone as mentioned in the original. He did not mention cleaning himself in al-Mabsut, but mentioned it in al-Siyar al-Kabir, and added in Nawadir Ibn Rushayd: and he performs wudu alone. Then some scholars said: what is meant by cleaning himself is complete purification, such that he cleans his private part alone without help. Others said: it means (cleaning) from impurity even if he cannot complete full purification, and that is understood from the apparent meaning of al-Khassaf's words. In Ghayat al-Bayan, al-Tabyin, and al-Kafi that the fatwa is on the saying of al-Khassaf of estimation by seven, because the father is commanded to order him to pray when he reaches it, and that is only if the child is with him. If they differ, the boy says I am seven and she says he is six, the judge does not swear either, but he looks: if he eats alone, dresses alone, and cleans himself alone, he is given; otherwise not, as in al-Zahiriyyah. And he sufficed with mentioning eating over drinking, so drinking was mentioned in al-Khulasah, and the four were combined in al-Tabyin. As for what is in Fath al-Qadir and al-Khulasah of not mentioning cleaning himself, that is an oversight. And the author, may Allah have mercy on him, indicated by mentioning the mother and grandmother that others are more entitled, so if he said 'and the custodian has more right until he becomes independent' it would have been clearer. · His statement: (And with her until she menstruates) meaning the mother and grandmother have more right to the young girl until she menstruates, because after independence she needs to learn the manners of women, and the woman is more capable of that. After puberty, she needs protection and preservation, and the father is stronger and more guiding in that. By this it is known that if he said 'until she reaches puberty' it would have been better. And from Muhammad that she is given to the father when she reaches the age of desire due to the need for protection. He said in al-Niqayah: and that is what is considered due to the corruption of the time. And in Nafaqat al-Khassaf: and from Abu Yusuf similar. And in al-Tabyin: and by this fatwa is given in our time. And the brother from father is more entitled than the maternal uncle because he is an agnate and closer. His statement: (He is given to the uterine brother etc.) It is mentioned in al-Fatawa al-Hindiyyah that the mother's father is more entitled than the uterine brother and the maternal uncle.
Source pages p. 287

Commentary
This passage explains the duration of custody for the mother and grandmother. For a male child, they retain custody until he becomes independent (yastaghni), which is estimated at seven years of age according to al-Khassaf's view, which is the relied-upon fatwa. The criterion is that the child can independently eat, drink, dress, and clean himself (istinja). There is some difference about whether he must also perform wudu alone. The fatwa prefers the age of seven because the father is then responsible for the child's prayer. If the parents dispute the child's age, the judge examines the child's actual abilities rather than swearing them. For a female child, custody lasts until she menstruates (i.e., reaches puberty). However, there is a view from Imam Muhammad that she is given to the father when she reaches the age of sexual desire (hadd al-shahwa) due to the need for protection, and this is the operative fatwa in later times because of moral corruption. The passage ends with a note that a paternal half-brother is preferred over a maternal uncle, and according to al-Fatawa al-Hindiyyah, the mother's father (maternal grandfather) is preferred over the uterine brother and maternal uncle.

Key Terms
حضانة (hadanah): Custody of a child, including physical care and upbringing.
استغناء (istighna'): The child's ability to independently perform basic tasks without assistance.
حد الشهوة (hadd al-shahwah): The age at which a girl begins to feel sexual desire, roughly 9-10 years.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the later fatwa mentioned in this passage, when does custody of a girl shift from mother to father?
A) When she turns seven
B) When she menstruates
C) When she reaches the age of desire
D) When she becomes independent

Key Takeaway
The duration of mother's custody differs for boys and girls, and the Hanafi school's fatwa on girls shifted to earlier age due to societal change.

Custody of a Boy: Mother and Grandmother's Right Until Independence
Ruling on mother's custody with estimation of seven years

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the mother's and grandmother's right to custody of a boy and explain the estimation of seven years for his independence.

Core Idea
A boy remains with his mother or grandmother until he can eat, drink, dress, and clean himself alone – estimated at seven years.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq explains the key ruling on custody (hadanah) for a boy. The mother and grandmother hold the primary right until the child reaches a stage of self-sufficiency. The text also clarifies the order of other custodians when no agnate is present and how to resolve disputes about the child's age. Understanding this ruling helps in determining the line between maternal and paternal care in the Hanafi school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the main ruling
The text states: 'The mother and grandmother have more right to the boy until he becomes independent.' Identify who is entitled and until when.
2
Understand the estimation of independence
The text estimates independence at seven years based on al-Khassaf. Note the reasoning: a seven-year-old can manage basic tasks alone.
3
Examine the conditions for independence
The text lists four things the child must do alone: eating, drinking, dressing, and cleaning. Note that some scholars add wudu.
4
Note the intra-Hanafi dispute
Some scholars define independence by capability rather than fixed age. The relied-upon position (fatwa) is the seven-year estimation.
5
Consider the order of other custodians
The text also explains the sequence when there is no agnate: maternal brother, his son, etc., and how to prefer among equals.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الطلاق باب الحضانة
قالوا : إذا لم يكن للصغير عصبة يدفع إلى الأخ لأم ثم إلى ولده ثم إلى العم لأم ثم إلى الخال لأب وأم ثم لأب ثم لأم لأن لهؤلاء ولاية عند أبي حنيفة في النكاح. وبهذا علم أن مرادهم بذوي الأرحام هنا وفي باب ولاية إلا نكاح قرابة ليست بعصبة لا المذكور في الفرائض أنه قريب ليس بذي سهم ولا عصبة لأن بعض أقارب الفروض داخل في ذوي الأرحام هنا كالأخ لأم، وإذا اجتمع مستحقو الحضانة في درجة كالإخوة والأعمام فأصلحهم أولى، فإن تساووا فأورعهم، فإن تساووا فأسنهم. وفي البدائع لا حق للرجال من قبل الأم وهو محمول على ما إذا كان من قبل الأب من هو موجود قوله : (والأم والجدة أحق بالغلام حتى يستغني وقدر بسبع لأنه إذا استغنى يحتاج إلى تأديب والتخلق بأداب الرجال وأخلاقهم والأب أقدر على التأديب والتعنيف، وما ذكره المصنف من التقدير قول الخصاف اعتباراً بسبع للقالب لأن الظاهر أن الصغير إذا بلغ السبع يهتدي بنفسه إلى الأكل والشرب واللبس والاستنجاء وحده فلا حاجة إلى الحضانة فلا مخالفة بين تقدير الاستغناء بالسن وبين أن على الأشياء الأربعة وحده كما هو المذكور في الأصل، ولم يذكر الاستنجاء في المبسوط وذكره في السير الكبير وزاد في نوادر ابن رشيد ويتوضأ وحده ثم من المشايخ من قال : المراد من الاستنجاء تمام الطهارة بأن يطهر وجهه وحده بلا معين. ومنهم من قال بل من النجاسة وإن لم يقدر على تمام الطهارة وهو المفهوم من ظاهر كلام الخصاف. وفي غاية البيان والتبيين والكافي أن الفتوى على قول الخصاف من التقدير بالسبع لأن الأب مأمور بأن يأمره بالصلاة إذا بلغها وإنما يكون ذلك إذا كان الولد عنده . ولو اختلفا فقال ابن وقالت سبع ابن ست لا يحلف القاضي أحدهما ولكن ينظر إن كان يأكل وحده ويلبس وحده ويستنجي وحده دفع وإلا فلا كذا في الظهيرية. واستغنى بذكر الأكل عن الشرب ولذا ذكر الشرب في الخلاصة وجمع بين الأربعة في التبيين وأما ما في فتح القدير والخلاصة من عدم ذكر الاستنجاء فسهو. وأشار المصنف رحمه الله بذكر الأم والجدة إلى أن غيرهما أولى، فلو قال والحاضنة أحق به حتى يستغني لكان أصرح.
Book of Divorce, Chapter of Custody. They said: If the young child has no agnate, he is handed over to the maternal brother, then to his son, then to the paternal uncle through the mother, then to the maternal uncle through father and mother, then through father, then through mother, because these have guardianship according to Abu Hanifa in marriage. By this it is known that their intent by 'dhawu al-arham' here and in the chapter of guardianship except marriage is a relative who is not an agnate, not the one mentioned in inheritance as a relative who has neither a prescribed share nor is an agnate, because some prescribed share relatives are included in dhawu al-arham here, like the maternal brother. And when entitled custodians are equal in degree, such as brothers and paternal uncles, the most righteous is preferable; if equal, the most God-fearing; if equal, the eldest. In al-Bada'i: Men from the mother's side have no right, and this is interpreted as when there exists someone from the father's side. His statement: (The mother and grandmother have more right to the boy until he becomes independent, and it is estimated at seven years, because when he becomes independent he needs discipline and to adopt the manners and ethics of men, and the father is more capable of discipline and sternness. And what the author mentioned of estimation is the statement of al-Khassaf, considering seven years as the default, because apparently a young child when he reaches seven years guides himself to eating, drinking, dressing, and cleaning himself alone, so there is no need for custody. So there is no contradiction between estimating independence by age and that he does the four things alone, as mentioned in al-Asl. And he did not mention cleaning in al-Mabsut, but mentioned it in al-Siyar al-Kabir, and added in Nawadir Ibn Rushayd: and he performs wudu alone. Then some scholars said: what is meant by cleaning is complete purification, that he cleans his private part alone without help. And some said: rather from impurity even if he cannot complete purification, and this is understood from the apparent meaning of al-Khassaf's statement. In Ghayat al-Bayan, al-Tabyin, and al-Kafi: The fatwa is according to al-Khassaf's statement of estimation by seven years, because the father is commanded to order him to pray when he reaches it, and that only happens when the child is with him. And if they disagree, saying he is seven or six, the judge does not swear either of them, but looks: if he eats alone, dresses alone, and cleans himself alone, he is handed over; otherwise not, as in al-Zahiriyyah. And he sufficed with mentioning eating over drinking, so drinking is mentioned in al-Khulasah, and the four are combined in al-Tabyin. And what is in Fath al-Qadir and al-Khulasah of not mentioning cleaning is an oversight. And the author, may Allah have mercy on him, indicated by mentioning the mother and grandmother that others have more right, so if he said 'and the custodian has more right to him until he becomes independent', it would be more explicit.
Source pages p. 287

Commentary
This passage is a ruling on the right of custody (hadanah) for a boy. The text first addresses the order of custodians when there is no agnate ('asaba). It lists relatives from the mother's side: maternal brother, his son, maternal uncle from mother, etc., because Abu Hanifa gives them guardianship in marriage. It clarifies that 'dhawu al-arham' here means non-agnate relatives, including those who have prescribed shares in inheritance (like maternal brother). When custodians are equal in degree, the most righteous is preferred, then the most God-fearing, then the eldest. Then it states the main ruling: The mother and grandmother (both paternal and maternal) have the strongest right to custody of a boy until he reaches an age of independence, estimated at seven years. The reasoning ('illa) is that after independence, the boy needs discipline and male upbringing, for which the father is better suited. The estimation of seven years comes from Imam al-Khassaf, based on the observable fact that a seven-year-old can typically eat, drink, dress, and clean himself alone. Some scholars argue over whether 'cleaning' includes full purification or only removal of impurity, but the relied-upon position (fatwa) is the estimation by seven years, supported by the hadith that a father is commanded to order his child to pray at seven. If the parents disagree on the child's age, the judge does not administer an oath but inspects the child's abilities. The author notes that his phrase 'mother and grandmother' might imply others are more rightful, so the expression 'custodian' would be clearer.

Key Terms
عصبة ('asabah): Agnate relative through the male line who inherits as residuary.
ذوي الأرحام (dhawu al-arham): Uterine relatives; blood relatives who are not agnates and not Quranic heirs.
حضانة (hadanah): The legal right and duty to physically care for and raise a young child.
استغناء (istighna'): The child's self-sufficiency in basic needs like eating, drinking, dressing, and cleaning.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon opinion (mufta bihi), at what age is a boy considered to have reached the age of independence (istighna') for the purpose of custody?
A) Six years
B) Seven years
C) Nine years
D) Until he reaches puberty

Key Takeaway
The mother and grandmother have the right to custody of a boy until he becomes independent, estimated at seven years based on his ability to manage basic tasks alone.
