كتاب الطلاق باب النفقة
قال عباراتهم . في البدائع : ولا خلاف بينهم في الطلاق على مال أنه لا يبرأ به عن سائر الحقوق التي وجبت لها بسبب النكاح .اهـ. فقد أفاد عدم سقوط النفقة والكسوة المفروضتين بالطلاق على مال لأنه صرح بسائر الحقوق وهي ثلاثة : المهر والنفقة والكسوة. ولا يمكن حمله على المهر فقط لأنه يبطل به قوله سائر الحقوق. وقال قبله وأما حكم الخلع فإن كان بغير بدل بأن قال خالعتك ونوى به الطلاق فحكمه أن يقع الطلاق ولا يسقط شيء من المهر والنفقة الماضية، وإن كان ببدل إلى آخره فهذا صريح في المسألة أيضاً، وفي غاية البيان: أما إذا كان العقد بلفظ الطلاق على مال فهل تقع البراءة عن الحقوق المتعلقة بالنكاح؟ ففي ظاهر الرواية لا تقع لأن لفظ الطلاق لا يدل على إسقاط الحق الواجب بالنكاح، وفي رواية الحسن عن أبي حنيفة تقع البراءة عنها لإتمام المقصود .اهـ وظاهره أن الطلاق إذا لم يكن على مال لا يسقط شيئاً من الحقوق الواجبة اتفاقاً فهذا كله يدل على ضعف الرواية السابقة خصوصاً أن مفهوم الكتب حجة، وقد قيدوا سقوطها بموت أحدهما وظاهر ما في الخانية والظهيرية أن الخصاف زاد الطلاق من عنده وليس له أصل في المذهب، فالذي يتعين المصير إليه على كل مفت وقاض اعتماد عدم السقوط خصوصاً ما تضمنه القول بالسقوط من الإضرار بالنساء حتى استفتيت وقت تأليف هذا المحل عن امرأة لها كسوة مفروضة تجمد لها عشر سنين ولم يدفع لها الزوج ثم إنها رفعته إلى قاض وحكم عليه بالدفع فاستمهلها يوماً ثم ذهب إلى قاضِ رومي وخلعها عنده بغير علمها فحكم له القاضي الحنفي بسقوط الكسوة الماضية، ولا يخفى من الضرر. فإن قلت: لم لم تعتمد على تصحيح الزيعلي بقوله «وكذا لا تسقط بالطلاق في الصحيح لما ذكرنا قلت لأن كلامه في النفقة المستدانة بأمر القاضي وكلامنا في ما في ذلك المفروضة فقط .
قوله : (ولا ترد (المعجلة أي لا ترد النفقة المعجلة بموت أحدهما ونحوه بأن عجل لها نفقة شهر بعد فرض القاضي أو التراضي ثم مات أحدهما أطلقه فشمل ما إذا كانت قائمة أو هالكة، فإن كانت هالكة فلا ترد شيئاً اتفاقاً، وإن كانت قائمة أو مستهلكة فكذلك عندهما. وقال محمد يحتسب لها نفقة ما مضى وما بقي فهو للزوج، وعلى هذا الخلاف
قوله : (هذه عبارتهما باللفظ) أي عبارة الخانية والظهيرية بلفظها من غير تغيير قوله : (قد أفتى به الشيخان) أي الصدر الشهيد وظهير الدين المرغيناني .
قوله : (فالذي يتعين المصير إليه الخ) سيرجح خلاف هذا عند قول المتن «ولمعتدة الطلاق» وأيضاً نازعه العلامة المقدسي في شرحه فبحث فيما ذكره من الأمر الأول بأن ما كل أحد يعلم هذا فيتوقف على أن يعلمه مفت ماجن وأيضاً يتوقف على أن يحكم به حنفي عالم بالشروط فقد يدعي عند شافعي ونحوه فيحكم لها باللزوم فيضيع ،طلاقه وفي الأمر الثاني بأن ما ذكره من أنه يسقط
Book of Divorce, Chapter of Maintenance: And just as fixed maintenance is cancelled by the death of one of the spouses, is it cancelled by divorce? They differed on it. Some said: It is not cancelled. And Judge Imam Abu Ali al-Nasafi said: I found a narration about its cancellation. And al-Baqqali mentioned that according to Muhammad it is cancelled, and there is no narration from Abu Yusuf. And Shams al-A'imma al-Hulwani mentioned that al-Khassaf added another cause for cancellation of fixed maintenance, saying: It is cancelled by his death and her death, and it is cancelled if he divorces her or severs her. This is their wording literally. In al-Khulasa and al-Bazzaziyya: Is fixed maintenance cancelled by divorce? It is related from Judge Imam Abu Ali al-Nasafi that it is cancelled, and in the Fatawa of al-Baqqali the difference between Abu Yusuf and Muhammad is mentioned. In al-Dhakhira: If the husband divorces her in this way, what has accrued of maintenance after the judge's decree is cancelled; so it is related from Judge Imam Abu Ali al-Nasafi. And he used to say: We found a narration of this issue in the book of the Judge. And al-Sadr al-Shahid and al-Shaykh al-Imam Zahir al-Din al-Marghinani used to give fatwa by it, analogizing to the dhimmi: if jizya has accrued on him and then he becomes Muslim, what had accrued is cancelled. The aspect of analogy is that the dhimmi is only taken jizya for persistence on false religion, and that meaning has ceased by Islam, so jizya is cancelled. Similarly here, the woman only deserves maintenance for the connection that was between them, and that connection has been severed by divorce. As for maintenance that was taken as a debt by order of the judge, it is not cancelled by divorce, and that is the correct view because it is like the husband borrowing himself. This is from al-Dhakhira. In al-Mujtaba: If the husband divorces her in these cases, what has accrued after the judge's decree is cancelled. So it is apparent from this that the preponderant view among them is its cancellation by divorce like death, especially since the two shaykhs gave fatwa accordingly as in al-Dhakhira. And the apparent meaning of their words is that there is no difference between revocable and irrevocable divorce because in the wording of al-Khaniyya and al-Zahiriyya they coupled irrevocable with divorce, so it is known that divorce... The weak slave said: The opinion of cancellation by divorce, even irrevocable, should be weak for several reasons: First: They agreed that he is imprisoned for fixed maintenance if he refuses to pay it, and if it were cancelled by divorce, he could divorce her so it is cancelled, then take her back. Second: They explicitly stated the permissibility of taking a guarantor for fixed maintenance for the period fixed by the judge, whereas guarantee is only valid for a sound debt. They said: It is only cancelled by payment or discharge. If the debt of maintenance were cancelled by divorce, it would not be sound, so guarantee for it would not be valid. And our case is not harmed by its cancellation by death of one of them because that is due to an accident, since its origin is a gift, and gifts are cancelled by death before taking possession. Third, and it is the strongest: What they mentioned in the chapter on khul': all of them mentioned that divorce for property does not cancel any of the rights of marriage, unlike khul' for property. And there is no harm in mentioning his saying: (Condition by death, etc.). Al-Ramli said: Our shaykh Muhammad ibn Siraj al-Hanuti conditioned cancellation by divorce if a month or more had passed, and that is a necessary condition. The debt. In al-Bada'i: There is no disagreement among them concerning divorce for property that he is not discharged by it from other rights that became due because of marriage. So this indicates the non-cancellation of fixed maintenance and clothing by divorce for property because he explicitly said 'other rights' which are three: dower, maintenance, and clothing. And it cannot be restricted to dower only because that would nullify his saying 'other rights'. And he said before: As for the ruling of khul': if it is without compensation, by saying 'I divorce you' (khala'tuk) and intending divorce, the ruling is that divorce occurs and nothing of dower or past maintenance is cancelled; if it is with compensation, etc. This is explicit on the issue as well. In Ghayat al-Bayan: As for when the contract is in the wording of divorce for property, is discharge from rights related to marriage effected? In the apparent narration (Zahir al-Riwaya) it is not effected because the word divorce does not indicate cancellation of a right due by marriage. In the narration of al-Hasan from Abu Hanifa, discharge is effected because the purpose is completed. The apparent meaning is that if divorce is not for property, no rights are cancelled by agreement. All this indicates the weakness of the previous narration, especially since the implication of the books is proof, and they conditioned cancellation by death of one of them. And what is apparent from al-Khaniyya and al-Zahiriyya is that al-Khassaf added divorce from himself and it has no basis in the madhhab. So what must be adopted by every mufti and judge is reliance on non-cancellation, especially what the opinion of cancellation entails of harm to women. Indeed, I was asked for a fatwa at the time of writing this section about a woman who had fixed clothing (maintenance) accrued for ten years, and her husband did not pay. Then she took him to a judge and he ordered him to pay. He asked for a day's respite, then went to a Roman judge and got a khul' from her without her knowledge. The Hanafi judge ruled that the past clothing was cancelled. And the harm is not hidden. If you say: Why did you not rely on al-Zayla'i's correction where he said 'Similarly, it is not cancelled by divorce according to the correct view as we mentioned'? I say: Because his words are about maintenance taken as a debt by order of the judge, and our words are about fixed maintenance only. His saying: (And prepaid is not returned) means prepaid maintenance is not returned upon death of one of them etc. If he prepaid her the maintenance of a month after the judge's decree or by mutual consent, then one of them died, it is general, including if it is still existing or destroyed. If it is destroyed, nothing is returned by agreement. If it is still existing or consumed, so according to them (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad). Muhammad said: It is counted as maintenance for what has passed, and what remains is for the husband. On this is the disagreement. His saying: (This is their wording literally) means the wording of al-Khaniyya and al-Zahiriyya literally without change. His saying: (The two shaykhs gave fatwa) means al-Sadr al-Shahid and Zahir al-Din al-Marghinani. His saying: (What must be adopted etc.) He will prefer the opposite of this at the statement of the matn 'And for the woman undergoing 'idda of divorce'. Also, the scholar al-Maqdisi disputed with him in his commentary and discussed what he mentioned in the first reason, saying that not everyone knows this, so it depends on a licentious mufti knowing it; also it depends on a Hanafi judge knowing the conditions, because she might claim before a Shafi'i or similar judge who would rule for its binding, so his divorce would be wasted. And in the second reason: what he mentioned about it being cancelled...

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq discusses a contested issue within the Hanafi school: whether maintenance that a judge has already fixed (al-nafaqah al-mufawwadah) is cancelled by divorce, similar to how it is cancelled by death of either spouse. The author first presents the views: some say it is not cancelled; Judge Abu Ali al-Nasafi reports a narration that it is cancelled; al-Baqqali mentions that according to Imam Muhammad it is cancelled but no narration from Abu Yusuf; al-Hulwani adds that al-Khassaf also included divorce as a cause for cancellation. The preponderant view among earlier scholars (like al-Sadr al-Shahid and al-Marghinani) was that cancellation occurs, by analogy with the jizya of a dhimmi who converts to Islam—just as jizya falls away when the reason (kufr) ceases, maintenance falls away when the marital bond (al-wuslah) is severed by divorce. However, the author ('the weak slave') argues that this view is weak and gives three reasons against it: (1) if divorce cancelled maintenance, a husband could divorce to avoid payment and then remarry, which contradicts the agreement that he is imprisoned for non-payment; (2) the law allows taking a guarantor for fixed maintenance, but a guarantee is only valid for a debt that cannot be cancelled arbitrarily—if divorce cancelled it, the debt would be unsound; (3) evidence from the chapter on khul' shows that divorce in exchange for property does not cancel any marital rights, including maintenance and clothing, so ordinary divorce (without exchange) should also not cancel them. He then cites al-Bada'i and other works confirming that divorce for property does not cancel rights, and that the apparent narration (Zahir al-Riwaya) is that no cancellation occurs. The author concludes that the correct and relied-upon position (al-mu'tamad) is that fixed maintenance is not cancelled by divorce, especially to prevent harm to women, and gives a real-life example of a woman who lost ten years of clothing maintenance due to a manipulative khul' arranged without her knowledge. He also clarifies that the view of non-cancellation applies only to maintenance that was already fixed by a judge; if it was taken as a loan by order of the judge, it is certainly not cancelled (al-sahih). Later marginal notes discuss a condition by al-Ramli about a month passing, and a rebuttal from al-Maqdisi regarding the practicality of the argument.

Key Terms
النفقة المفروضة (al-nafaqah al-mufawwadah): Maintenance that a judge has set at a specific amount or in a specific form (clothing, food, etc.) as a binding obligation on the husband.
الطلاق البائن (al-talaq al-bāʾin): Irrevocable divorce, after which the husband cannot take the wife back without a new marriage contract.
الكفيل (al-kafīl): A guarantor who undertakes to pay the maintenance debt if the husband fails.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon (mufta bihi) view in the Hanafi school, what happens to maintenance that a judge had fixed (al-nafaqah al-mufawwadah) if the husband divorces the wife?
A) It is cancelled immediately, like upon death.
B) It is not cancelled; the husband still owes it.
C) It is cancelled only if the divorce is revocable (rajʿī).
D) It is reduced by half.

Key Takeaway
Fixed maintenance is a sound debt that is not cancelled by divorce; only death, payment, or discharge ends it.

Talaq — Divorce
intermediate
12 min
Divorce on Payment Does Not Discharge Past Maintenance
Establishing that divorce on payment does not waive past marital rights.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on whether divorce on payment discharges past maintenance and identify the evidence from Zahir al-Riwaya.

Core Idea
Divorce on payment does not waive past maintenance rights.

This passage addresses a critical question in family law: does a divorce in which the wife agrees to pay compensation or forgo rights also wipe out past obligations like unpaid maintenance? The Hanafi school's answer, as established in Zahir al-Riwaya, is a clear no. We will follow the author's reasoning through key texts and see why a rare contrary narration is rejected.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core ruling
State the central claim: divorce on payment does not discharge past rights (nafaqah, kiswah, mahr).
The key phrase is 'لا يبرأ به عن سائر الحقوق'.
2
Locate the textual evidence
Find the primary sources: al-Bada'i (consensus) and Ghayat al-Bayan (Zahir al-Riwaya position).
The text explicitly lists the three rights.
3
Examine the intra-madhhab dispute
Note the rare narration from Hasan ibn Ziyad that discharge occurs, and understand why the author rejects it.
The author calls it weak and baseless.
4
Assess the authority weight
Recognize that Zahir al-Riwaya is the standard; the contrary narration is from nawadir and not relied upon.
Al-Khassaf's addition is said to have no basis.
5
Apply to a real case
Consider the author's fatwa story of a husband using a trick to drop past kiswah, illustrating the harm prevented by this ruling.
The judge's ruling in that case was wrong according to the mufta bihi.

قال عباراتهم . في البدائع : ولا خلاف بينهم في الطلاق على مال أنه لا يبرأ به عن سائر الحقوق التي وجبت لها بسبب النكاح .اهـ. فقد أفاد عدم سقوط النفقة والكسوة المفروضتين بالطلاق على مال لأنه صرح بسائر الحقوق وهي ثلاثة : المهر والنفقة والكسوة. ولا يمكن حمله على المهر فقط لأنه يبطل به قوله سائر الحقوق. وقال قبله وأما حكم الخلع فإن كان بغير بدل بأن قال خالعتك ونوى به الطلاق فحكمه أن يقع الطلاق ولا يسقط شيء من المهر والنفقة الماضية، وإن كان ببدل إلى آخره فهذا صريح في المسألة أيضاً، وفي غاية البيان: أما إذا كان العقد بلفظ الطلاق على مال فهل تقع البراءة عن الحقوق المتعلقة بالنكاح؟ ففي ظاهر الرواية لا تقع لأن لفظ الطلاق لا يدل على إسقاط الحق الواجب بالنكاح، وفي رواية الحسن عن أبي حنيفة تقع البراءة عنها لإتمام المقصود .اهـ وظاهره أن الطلاق إذا لم يكن على مال لا يسقط شيئاً من الحقوق الواجبة اتفاقاً فهذا كله يدل على ضعف الرواية السابقة خصوصاً أن مفهوم الكتب حجة، وقد قيدوا سقوطها بموت أحدهما وظاهر ما في الخانية والظهيرية أن الخصاف زاد الطلاق من عنده وليس له أصل في المذهب، فالذي يتعين المصير إليه على كل مفت وقاض اعتماد عدم السقوط خصوصاً ما تضمنه القول بالسقوط من الإضرار بالنساء حتى استفتيت وقت تأليف هذا المحل عن امرأة لها كسوة مفروضة تجمد لها عشر سنين ولم يدفع لها الزوج ثم إنها رفعته إلى قاض وحكم عليه بالدفع فاستمهلها يوماً ثم ذهب إلى قاضِ رومي وخلعها عنده بغير علمها فحكم له القاضي الحنفي بسقوط الكسوة الماضية، ولا يخفى من الضرر. فإن قلت: لم لم تعتمد على تصحيح الزيعلي بقوله «وكذا لا تسقط بالطلاق في الصحيح لما ذكرنا قلت لأن كلامه في النفقة المستدانة بأمر القاضي وكلامنا في المفروضة فقط .
He said their expressions: In al-Bada'i: There is no disagreement among them that in divorce on payment, he is not discharged from the rest of the rights that became obligatory due to marriage. End. So it indicates that the obligatory maintenance (nafaqah) and clothing (kiswah) are not cancelled by divorce on payment because he explicitly mentioned the rest of the rights, which are three: dower, maintenance, and clothing. It cannot be interpreted as only dower because that would nullify his statement 'the rest of the rights.' And before that he said: As for the ruling of khul', if it is without compensation by him saying 'I have divorced you (khala'tuki)' and he intended divorce by it, then its ruling is that divorce occurs and nothing of the past dower and maintenance is dropped. If it is with compensation, to the end. So this is explicit on the issue as well. And in Ghayat al-Bayan: If the contract is with the word of divorce on payment, does discharge from the rights related to marriage occur? In the apparent narration (Zahir al-Riwaya), it does not occur because the word of divorce does not indicate dropping the right owed due to marriage. In the narration of al-Hasan from Abu Hanifah, discharge from them occurs to complete the purpose. End. And its apparent meaning is that if divorce is not on payment, nothing from the obligatory rights is dropped by agreement. All this indicates the weakness of the previous narration, especially since the concept of the books is a proof, and they restricted its dropping to the death of one of them. And apparent in al-Khaniyya and al-Zahiriyya that al-Khassaf added divorce from himself and it has no basis in the madhhab. So what is determined for every mufti and judge is to rely on non-dropping, especially what the statement of dropping entails of harm to women, until I was asked for a fatwa at the time of composing this passage about a woman who had obligatory clothing accrued for ten years without the husband paying, then she brought him to a judge who ordered him to pay, so he asked for a day's respite then went to a Roman judge and had her divorced (khul') there without her knowledge, so the Hanafi judge ruled for dropping the past clothing. The harm is not hidden. If you say: Why did you not rely on the correction of al-Zayla'i with his statement 'And likewise it does not drop by divorce in the correct view due to what we mentioned'? I say: Because his words are about maintenance borrowed by the judge's order, and our words are only about the obligatory (past) maintenance.
Source pages p. 322

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof from the Hanafi school that divorce on payment (talaq 'ala mal) does not discharge the husband from past maintenance obligations (nafaqah and kiswah). The author begins by citing al-Bada'i, which states there is no disagreement that divorce on payment does not release the husband from other marital rights. These rights are three: mahr (dower), nafaqah (maintenance), and kiswah (clothing). The text emphasizes that the phrase 'other rights' cannot be restricted to only mahr. Then it mentions khul' (divorce initiated by wife) without compensation: divorce occurs but nothing of past rights is dropped. For khul' with compensation, it is similar. Al-Ghaya al-Bayan is quoted, showing that in Zahir al-Riwaya, discharge from rights does not occur because the word 'talaq' does not imply waiver of rights. However, there is a rare narration from Hasan ibn Ziyad from Abu Hanifa that discharge does occur to complete the purpose. The author argues this narration is weak, as it contradicts the principle that rights only drop by death of one spouse, and al-Khassaf's addition has no basis. He strongly recommends that muftis and judges adopt the position of non-dropping, citing harm to women. He narrates a real case where a husband used a trick (hila) by going to a non-Hanafi judge to drop past kiswah. The author clarifies that al-Zayla'i's correction about maintenance refers to borrowed maintenance, not the obligatory past maintenance. The authority weight is Zahir al-Riwaya, and the mufta bihi position is non-dropping.

Key Terms
الطلاق على مال (al-talaq 'ala mal): Divorce where the wife agrees to pay compensation (or forgo rights) in exchange for the husband pronouncing divorce.
البراءة عن الحقوق (al-bara'ah 'an al-huquq): Release from marital rights (mahr, nafaqah, kiswah) that accrued during marriage.
ظاهر الرواية (Zahir al-Riwayah): The established transmitted rulings of the school from Abu Hanifa and his students, as recorded by Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, if a husband divorces his wife in exchange for her waiving maintenance, does the divorce itself discharge the past years of unpaid maintenance?
A) Yes, because the wife agreed to the divorce.
B) No, because the word 'talaq' does not waive past rights.
C) Yes, because it is a form of khul'.
D) No, only if the wife explicitly forgives the debt.

Key Takeaway
Past maintenance remains a debt after divorce on payment; the rare contrary narration is not relied upon.

Advance Maintenance Not Returned Upon Death or Divorce
Ruling on advance nafaqah not returned upon death or divorce

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on advance nafaqah upon death and explain the intra-madhhab dispute between Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani.

Core Idea
Advance nafaqah is a gift — once delivered, it is not returned upon death.

Imagine a husband pays his wife the full month's maintenance at the beginning of the month. If the husband dies on day five, does the wife need to return the remaining twenty-five days' worth? The Hanafi school addresses this with a clear position: the advance payment is a gift (silah), not a loan. This lesson unpacks the ruling, the internal dispute, and the operative fatwa.

Guided Path
1
Identify the legal issue
Recognize that the issue is the fate of advance nafaqah when one spouse dies: is it returned or retained?
This is a dispute about the nature of the payment: gift or consideration.
2
Locate the Hanafi position and its basis
The main position (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) holds that it is a gift (silah); once delivered, ownership is established and not revoked by death.
Analogy to hibah: gifts are irrevocable after delivery.
3
Identify the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Muhammad al-Shaybani argued for proportionate return: wife keeps only for days used, the rest belongs to husband's heirs.
He analogized to salary of a judge or soldier; entitlement ends with right to confinement.
4
Determine the mufta bibi and tarjih
The fatwa is on the view of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (Sahibayn), specifically Abu Yusuf according to al-Walwaliji.
Authority weight: Zahir al-Riwayah.
5
Consider the thamarah al-khilaf
Practical difference: if husband dies after advance payment, wife keeps the entire amount under the fatwa, not proportionate.
This applies even if the money is still in hand or partially consumed.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (ولا ترد (المعجلة) أي لا ترد النفقة المعجلة بموت أحدهما ونحوه بأن عجل لها نفقة شهر بعد فرض القاضي أو التراضي ثم مات أحدهما أطلقه فشمل ما إذا كانت قائمة أو هالكة، فإن كانت هالكة فلا ترد شيئاً اتفاقاً، وإن كانت قائمة أو مستهلكة فكذلك عندهما. وقال محمد يحتسب لها نفقة ما مضى وما بقي فهو للزوج، وعلى هذا الخلاف قوله : (هذه عبارتهما باللفظ) أي عبارة الخانية والظهيرية بلفظها من غير تغيير قوله : (قد أفتى به الشيخان) أي الصدر الشهيد وظهير الدين المرغيناني . قوله : (فالذي يتعين المصير إليه الخ) سيرجح خلاف هذا عند قول المتن «ولمعتدة الطلاق» وأيضاً نازعه العلامة المقدسي في شرحه فبحث فيما ذكره من الأمر الأول بأن ما كل أحد يعلم هذا فيتوقف على أن يعلمه مفت ماجن وأيضاً يتوقف على أن يحكم به حنفي عالم بالشروط فقد يدعي عند شافعي ونحوه فيحكم لها باللزوم فيضيع ،طلاقه وفي الأمر الثاني بأن ما ذكره من أنه يسقط الكسوة لأنها استعجلت عوضاً عما تستحقه عليه بالاحتباس وقد بطل الاستحقاق بالموت فبطل العوض بقدره كرزق القاضي ورزق المقاتلة ولهما أنها صلة وقد اتصل بها القبض ولا رجوع في الصلات بعد الموت لانتهاء حكمها كما في الهبة وفتح القدير، والفتوى على قولهما، وجعله الولوالجي وأصحاب الفتاوى قول أبي يوسف قالوا والفتوى عليه. وشمل ما إذا كان المعجل الزوج أو أباه لما في الولوالجية وغيرها : أبو الزوج إذا دفع نفقة امرأة ابنه صرح بالوفاة اتفاقاً يكفينا مؤنة رده فيقال له لو كان يسقط بالموت لما صح التكفيل به فنقول : كان القياس ذلك لكن استحسن صحة التكفيل شفقة عليهن وامتثالاً لوصية الشارع بهن فذا مما خرج عن الأصل ضرورة، وجعله الموت من العوارض دون الطلاق تحكم بلا ريب .
His statement: 'And the advance (payment) is not returned' means the advance nafaqah is not returned due to the death of one of them or similar, such as if he advanced her nafaqah of a month after the judge's assessment or mutual agreement, then one of them died. He (the author) made it absolute so it includes whether it (the money) still exists or is destroyed. If it is destroyed, nothing is returned by agreement. If it exists or is consumed, likewise according to them (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad). And Muhammad said: She is credited for the nafaqah of what passed, and what remains belongs to the husband. And on this difference is his statement: 'These are their expressions by wording.' i.e. the wording of al-Khaniyya and al-Zahiriyya without change. His statement: 'The two shaykhs gave fatwa with it': i.e. al-Sadr al-Shahid and Zahir al-Din al-Marghinani. His statement: 'So what is determined to rely on etc.' He will later preponderate the opposite at the statement of the matn 'and for the divorced woman undergoing iddah' and also the 'Allamah al-Maqdisi contested him in his commentary and discussed what he mentioned of the first issue: that not everyone knows this, so it depends on it being known by a corrupt mufti, and it also depends on it being ruled by a Hanafi knowledgeable of the conditions, for he might claim before a Shafi'i etc. and she would be ruled for binding (payment). And in the second issue: that what he mentioned that the clothing drops because she hastened to take a substitute for what she deserved from him due to confinement, and the entitlement became void by death, so the substitute is cancelled proportionally like the salary of a judge and the pay of fighters. And according to them (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad): it is a gift and receipt has come, and there is no return in gifts after death because their ruling ends, like in a gift. And al-Isfandiyari and Fath al-Qadir: And the fatwa is according to them (Sahibayn). And al-Walwaliji and the authors of fatwa considered it the saying of Abu Yusuf, and they said: the fatwa is upon it. It includes whether the one who advanced is the husband or his father, as in al-Walwalijiyya and others: The husband's father if he paid the nafaqah of his son's wife, it is explicitly by death by agreement. It suffices us from the trouble of refuting it. It is said to him: If it was dropped by death, then the guarantee (takfil) with it would not be valid. So we say: By analogy that would be the case, but istihsan (juristic preference) allows the validity of the guarantee out of compassion for them and in compliance with the Prophet's advice regarding them. This is something that deviated from the original out of necessity. And making death one of the occurrences without divorce is arbitrary without doubt.
Source pages p. 322

Commentary
This passage is a ruling on advance nafaqah (nafaqah mu'ajjala) — when a husband pays maintenance in advance (e.g., for a month) and then one spouse dies. The question is whether the wife must return the remaining portion. The commentary begins by explaining the matn text 'and the advance is not returned.' The author notes that if the money is destroyed, there is agreement it is not returned. If it remains or is consumed, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad say it is not returned, while Muhammad has a variant: she is credited for the days she actually used, and the rest belongs to the husband. The fatwa is generally on the view of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (or specifically Abu Yusuf) that it is a gift (silah) and not returned after death, similar to a hibah (gift). The author then mentions a case where the husband's father paid nafaqah; the same rule applies. He defends the position that death does not void the gift, while divorce might be different. The authority weight is Zahir al-Riwaya, and the mufta bihi is that advance nafaqah is not returned upon death.

Key Terms
النفقة المعجلة (al-nafaqah al-mu'ajjalah): Maintenance paid in advance for a future period, typically a month.
صلة (silah): A gift given as a voluntary offering, not as a required payment.
حكم (hukm): The legal ruling or effect; here, the ruling of a gift ends upon death.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a husband gives his wife advanced nafaqah for a month, and the wife dies after ten days, what happens to the remaining advance according to the fatwa?
A) The wife's heirs must return the remaining twenty days' worth.
B) The husband can take it back because the contract ended.
C) The wife had already received it as a gift; it is not returned.
D) It is divided proportionally between the husband and the wife's heirs.

Key Takeaway
Advance nafaqah is a gift; once delivered, it is not returned upon death, per the Hanafi fatwa.

Discharge of Past Maintenance by Talaq: Intra-Hanafi Dispute and Fatwa Nuance
Author's response to al-Maqdisi's objections on maintenance discharge.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to analyze the differing positions among later Hanafi jurists on whether revocable talaq discharges past maintenance and apply the author's cautionary approach to fatwa practice.

Core Idea
Past maintenance remains a debt; later Hanafi opinions vary on discharge by revocable talaq—caution is paramount.

This lesson unpacks a critical debate among later Hanafi scholars: can revocable talaq (talaq raj'i) be used to discharge a husband's obligation to pay past maintenance? While the earlier Zahir al-Riwaya position holds that maintenance debts are not dropped, several later jurists permitted it in certain circumstances. The author, Ibn Nujaym, responds to three objections raised by al-Maqdisi and navigates the conflicting fatwa practice. By the end, you will understand the nuanced methodology required when issuing fatwa in such contested matters.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core issue
The passage addresses whether a revocable talaq (ṭalāq rajʿī) can discharge past maintenance obligations (nafaqah). Focus on the specific legal question: does the act of divorce itself amount to a waiver of the wife's right to past subsistence?
This is distinct from the question of future maintenance during ʿiddah, which is generally agreed to be due.
2
Examine the three objections of al-Maqdisi
Al-Maqdisi raised three criticisms against the non-dropping view. First, the term 'sa'ir al-huquq' (all other rights) in al-Bada'i might imply universality. Second, the rights that are not dropped could be narrowly interpreted. Third, the attribution of a contrary narration to al-Khassaf is an unfair slander. The author refutes each objection, showing that the non-dropping view has solid textual foundations.
Note the author's linguistic argument that 'sa'ir' can be used in a particular sense (salb al-ʿumūm), not necessarily universal denial.
3
Map the differing Hanafi positions
Identify the scholars who allowed dropping (e.g., al-Sadr al-Shahid, al-Marghinani, al-Ramli) and those who restricted or rejected it (e.g., the author, al-Shurunbulali). Note the range: some limited dropping to revocable talaq, others applied it absolutely. This is an intra-madhhab dispute (ikhtilaf fi al-madhhab).
The passage mentions that al-Qahistani confined dropping to revocable talaq, while al-Ramli gave fatwa of dropping absolutely.
4
Analyze the author's conclusion and methodology
Ibn Nujaym ultimately recommends 'tā'ammul ʿinda al-fatwā' (reflection at the time of fatwa). He does not definitively rule one way but urges the mufti to examine the husband's specific circumstances—whether his intent is to evade maintenance or due to the wife's misconduct. This reflects a cautious, case-by-case approach.
Notice the reference to Khizanat al-Muftin and Jawahir al-Fatawa as later sources that affirm the non-dropping view, but the debate remains open.
5
Apply the lesson to contemporary fatwa practice
Consider a modern scenario where a husband initiates a revocable divorce and claims that his duty to pay past maintenance is discharged. A mufti following this debate must weigh the conflicting authorities and investigate the husband's intentions to avoid injustice.
This step bridges the classical discussion to practical ifta'.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفي الثالث بأن قوله «أنه في البدائع بأنه يبطل سائر الحقوق مردود لأن سائر» يجيء بمعنى جميع فتكون القضية جزئية قصد بها سلب العموم لا عموم السلب ويكفي فيه تعلقه بالمهر فقط، وأيضاً يمكن حمل الحقوق التي لا تسقط بالطلاق على المهر ونفقة ما دون الشهر ونفقة استدين عليها بأمر فلا يبعد إطلاق جميع الحقوق عليها ثم قال : ثم إن نسبته الخصاف إلى زاد الطلاق من عنده أن أراد أنه لم يستنبطه من كلام المشايخ المتقدمين وأصولهم المعتمدة فهو جراءة عظيمة على هذا الإمام الذي قال عنه الإمام الحلواني إنه كبير في العلم يليق الاقتداء به والذي يتعين المصير إليه أن يقال يتأمل عند الفتوى كما يقع وجرت به عادة المشايخ رحمهم الله تعالى في هذا المقام فإن هذه الرواية لم يظهر ضعفها، كيف وقد أفتى بها الشيخان الصدر الشهيد والمرغيناني وذكرت في المتون كالوقاية والنقاية والإصلاح والغرر وغيرها، وظهر ضعف الوجوه التي قوى بها خلاف تلك الرواية ولهذا توقفت كثيراً في الفتوى بالسقوط مع ما ظهر لي من الأبحاث المذكورة وظفرت بنقل صريح في تصحيح عدم السقوط في خزانة المفتين فليتأمل عند الفتوى وفي الجواهر : إنه لا ينبغي أن يفتي بسقوطها بالطلاق الرجعي لئلا يتخذها الناس وسيلة لقطع حق النساء .اهـ. كلام المقدسي رحمه الله تعالى. فقد رجع إلى ما قاله المؤلف رحمه الله وإن قال أخوه في النهر فيه نظر وبين وجهه الرسلي ببعض ما مر وقال: إن المؤلف قد أفتى في فتاويه بالسقوط .اهـ. والذي اعتمده في منح الغفار ما في جواهر الفتاوى . من أن الفتوى السقوط بالرجعي واقتصر عليه القهستاني. وقال الشيخ علاء الدين: واستحسنه محشي الأشباه. وبالسقوط مطلقاً أفتى شيخنا الرملي لكن صحح الشرنبلالي في شرحه للوهبانية ما بحثه في البحر قال : وهو الأصح . ورد ما ذكره ابن الشحنة فتأمل عند الفتوى .اهـ. وهو يشعر بميله إلى ما بحثه المؤلف، وقد علمت تصحيحه وعبارة الزيلعي محتملة لأن يكون المراد بما صححه هو. هذا كما فهمه الشرنبلالي فاستدل بها وليست صريحة فيما حمله عليها المؤلف بل المتبادر منها الأول لما يعلم من مراجعتها. والحاصل أنه قد اختلف الإفتاء والتصحيح في هذه المسألة فينبغي كما قال بعض الفضلاء أن يتأمل عند الفتوى بأن ينظر في حال الرجل هل فعل ذلك تخلصاً من النفقة أو لسوء اخلاقها مثلاً.
And in the third (objection): that his statement 'that in al-Bada'i it nullifies the rest of the rights' is rejected because 'the rest' (sa'ir) comes in the meaning of 'all', so the proposition is particular intended to deny universality, not the universality of denial, and it suffices for it to be related to dower only. Also, the rights that are not dropped by divorce can be interpreted as dower and maintenance for less than a month and maintenance borrowed by order, so it is not unlikely to apply all rights to them. Then he said: Then his attribution of al-Khassaf to adding divorce from himself — if he meant that he did not derive it from the statements of the earlier scholars and their relied-upon principles, then it is a great audacity against this Imam about whom Imam al-Halwani said he is great in knowledge worthy of being followed. And what is determined to say is that one should reflect at the time of giving fatwa, as it occurs and the custom of the scholars has been in this matter. For this narration has not shown its weakness; how can it be when the two shaykhs (al-Sadr al-Shahid and al-Marghinani) gave fatwa with it, and it is mentioned in the texts like al-Wiqaya, al-Niqaya, al-Islah, al-Ghurar, and others. And the weakness of the aspects that strengthen the opposite of that narration has appeared. Therefore, I have hesitated a lot in giving fatwa of dropping, despite what appeared to me from the mentioned investigations, and I found an explicit transmission affirming non-dropping in Khizanat al-Muftin. So let one reflect at the time of giving fatwa. And in al-Jawahir: It is not proper to give fatwa of its dropping by revocable divorce lest people take it as a means to cut off women's rights. End. The statement of al-Maqdisi (may Allah have mercy on him) then he reverted to what the author said. And though his brother said in al-Nahr it has consideration, and al-Rasli explained it with some of what passed, saying that the author gave fatwa of dropping in his fatawa. But what is relied upon in Manh al-Ghaffar is what is in Jawahir al-Fatawa: that the fatwa is dropping for revocable divorce, and al-Qahistani limited it to that. And Shaykh Ala al-Din said: And the commentator of al-Ashbah considered it good. And our teacher al-Ramli gave fatwa of dropping absolutely, but al-Shurunbulali in his commentary on al-Wahbaniyya corrected what was discussed in al-Bahr, saying it is the most correct. And he refuted what Ibn al-Shihna mentioned. So reflect at the time of giving fatwa. End. And it indicates his inclination to what the author discussed, and you have known its correction. And the expression of al-Zayla'i is probable that what he corrected is this, as al-Shurunbulali understood it and used it as evidence, but it is not explicit in what the author interpreted. Rather, the apparent meaning from it is the first thing, as is known from reviewing it. The bottom line is that the fatwa and correction have differed in this issue, so some scholars have said one should reflect at the time of giving fatwa, considering the husband's situation: did he do that to escape maintenance or due to her bad character, etc.
Source pages p. 323

Commentary
This passage is a critical refinement by the author (Ibn Nujaym) responding to objections raised by al-Maqdisi against the ruling that talaq does not drop past maintenance. Al-Maqdisi had three objections: (1) that the word 'sā'ir' can mean all, but the proposition is particular; (2) that the rights that don't drop can be interpreted narrowly; (3) the attribution to al-Khassaf is a slander. The author defends the view of non-dropping but acknowledges that the issue is not settled. He cites authorities who gave fatwa of dropping (like al-Sadr al-Shahid and al-Marghinani), and mentions that al-Qahistani and others limited dropping to revocable divorce. He concludes that the fatwa is disputed, and recommends that the mufti consider the specific circumstances of the husband's intention. The key takeaway is that despite strong arguments for non-dropping, the practical fatwa is not uniform, and one must be cautious. The authority weight here is from later fatawa collections, not necessarily Zahir al-Riwaya.

Key Terms
الطلاق الرجعي (al-talaq al-rij'i): Revocable divorce where the husband can take back his wife during the iddah without a new contract.
سائر الحقوق (sa'ir al-huquq): All other marital rights (mahr, nafaqah, kiswah).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

B) Difference over whether talaq revocable or irrevocable can cause discharge.
C) There is no disagreement; all agree it does not drop.
D) Disagreement over the definition of al-kiswah.

Key Takeaway
The discharge of past maintenance by talaq remains a disputed issue; a mufti must examine the husband's circumstances and avoid generalizations.
